<p>The <b>Samsung Galaxy S III</b> (or <b>Galaxy S3</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">multi-touch</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slate_phone" title="Slate phone">slate</a>-format <a href="/wiki/Smartphone" title="Smartphone">smartphone</a> model designed, developed, and marketed by <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Electronics" title="Samsung Electronics">Samsung Electronics</a> that runs the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> <a href="/wiki/Operating_system" title="Operating system">OS</a> by <a href="/wiki/Google" title="Google">Google</a>. Launched in 2012, it had sold about 70 million units by 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-computerworld_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>It has additional software features, expanded hardware, and a redesigned physique from its predecessor, the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S_II" title="Samsung Galaxy S II">Samsung Galaxy S II</a>. The "S III" employs an <a href="/wiki/Intelligent_personal_assistant" title="Intelligent personal assistant">intelligent personal assistant</a> (<a href="/wiki/S_Voice" title="S Voice">S Voice</a>), eye-tracking ability, and increased storage. Although a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wireless_energy_transfer" title="Wireless energy transfer">wireless charging</a> option was announced, it never came to fruition. Depending on country, the 4.8-inch (120 mm) smartphone comes with different processors and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RAM" title="RAM">RAM</a> capacity, and <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The device was launched with <a href="/wiki/Android_Ice_Cream_Sandwich" title="Android Ice Cream Sandwich">Android 4.0.4 "Ice Cream Sandwich"</a>, was updated to <a href="/wiki/Android_Jelly_Bean" title="Android Jelly Bean">Android 4.3 "Jelly Bean"</a>, and can be updated to <a href="/wiki/Android_KitKat" title="Android KitKat">Android 4.4 "KitKat"</a> on variants with 2 GB of RAM. The phone's successor, the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S4" title="Samsung Galaxy S4">Samsung Galaxy S4</a>, was announced on 14 March 2013 and was released the following month.</p>
<p>Following an 18-month development phase, Samsung unveiled the S III on 3 May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMHS3launch_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMHS3launch-13">[13]</a></sup> The device was released in 28 European and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Middle_Eastern" title="Middle Eastern">Middle Eastern</a> countries on 29 May 2012, before being progressively released in other major markets in June 2012. Prior to release, 9 million pre-orders were placed by more than 100 <a href="/wiki/Mobile_network_operator" title="Mobile network operator">carriers</a> globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The S III was released by approximately 300 carriers in nearly 150 countries at the end of July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReutersS3release_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersS3release-4">[4]</a></sup> More than 20 million units of the S III were sold within the first 100 days of release<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100days20mil_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-100days20mil-15">[15]</a></sup> and more than 50 million until April 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50_million_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-50_million-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Because of overwhelming demand and a manufacturing problem with the blue variant of the phone,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geek_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-Geek-17">[17]</a></sup> there was an extensive shortage of the S III, especially in the United States. Nevertheless, the S III was well-received commercially and critically, with some technology commentators touting it as the "<a href="/wiki/IPhone" title="IPhone">iPhone</a> killer". In September 2012, <a href="/wiki/TechRadar" title="TechRadar">TechRadar</a> ranked it as the No. 1 handset in its constantly updated list of the 20 best mobile phones,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beavis.2C_Gareth_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Beavis.2C_Gareth-18">[18]</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Stuff_(magazine)" title="Stuff (magazine)">Stuff</a> magazine likewise ranked it at No. 1 in its list of 10 best smartphones in May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_10_Smartphones_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-Top_10_Smartphones-19">[19]</a></sup> The handset also won the "European Mobile Phone of 2012–13" award from the <a href="/wiki/European_Imaging_and_Sound_Association" title="European Imaging and Sound Association">European Imaging and Sound Association</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mobile_Devices_Awards_History_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mobile_Devices_Awards_History-20">[20]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/T3_(magazine)" title="T3 (magazine)"><i>T3</i> magazine</a>'s "Phone of the Year" award for 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Future_Publishing_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-Future_Publishing-21">[21]</a></sup> It played a major role in boosting Samsung's record <a href="/wiki/Earnings_before_interest_and_taxes" title="Earnings before interest and taxes">operating profit</a> during the second quarter of 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> As of November 2012<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the S III is part of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apple_Inc._v._Samsung_Electronics_Co.,_Ltd." title="Apple Inc. v. Samsung Electronics Co., Ltd.">high-profile lawsuit</a> between Samsung and <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In November 2012, research firm Strategy Analytics announced that the S III had overtaken Apple's <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4S" title="IPhone 4S">iPhone 4S</a> to become the world's best-selling smartphone model in Q3 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014, following the release of its former <a href="/wiki/Core_product" title="Core product">flagship</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxy_S5" title="Galaxy S5">Galaxy S5</a>, Samsung released a refreshed version called the "Galaxy S3 Neo" which has a <a href="/wiki/Multi-core_processor" title="Multi-core processor">quad-core</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snapdragon_400" title="Snapdragon 400">Snapdragon 400</a> processor clocked either at 1.2 or 1.4 GHz. It has 1.5 GB of RAM, 16 GB of internal storage and ships with Android 4.4.4 "KitKat".</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Design work on the S III started in late 2010 under the supervision of Chang Dong-hoon, Samsung's Vice President and Head of the Design Group of Samsung Electronics. From the start, the design group concentrated on a trend which Samsung dubs "organic", which suggests that a prospective design should reflect natural elements such as the flow of water and wind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design_story_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Design_story-25">[25]</a></sup> Some of the results of this design were the curved outline of the phone and its home screen's "Water Lux" effect, where taps and slides produce water ripples.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design_story_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Design_story-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Throughout the eighteen-month design process, Samsung implemented stringent security measures and procedures to maintain <a href="/wiki/Trade_secret" title="Trade secret">secrecy of the eventual design</a> until its launch. Designers worked on three <a href="/wiki/Prototype" title="Prototype">prototypes</a> concurrently while regarding each of them as the final product. Doing so required a constant duplication of effort, as they had to repeat the same process for all three prototypes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheInquirer_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-TheInquirer-27">[27]</a></sup> The prototypes, of which taking photos was forbidden, were locked in a separate laboratory, accessible only by core designers. They were transported by trusted company employees, instead of <a href="/wiki/Third-party_logistics" title="Third-party logistics">third-party couriers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TheInquirer_27-1"><a href="#cite_note-TheInquirer-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> "Because we were only permitted to see the products and others weren't," explained Principal Engineer Lee Byung-Joon, "we couldn't send <a href="/wiki/Blueprint" title="Blueprint">pictures or drawings</a>. We had to explain the Galaxy S III with all sorts of words."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Despite such security measures, specifications of one of the three units were leaked by <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">Vietnamese</a> Web site Tinhte, although it was not the selected design.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>Speculation in the general public and media outlets regarding the handset's specifications began gathering momentum several months before its formal unveiling in May 2012. In February 2012, prior to the <a href="/wiki/Mobile_World_Congress" title="Mobile World Congress">Mobile World Congress</a> (MWC) in <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, there were rumors that the handset would incorporate a 1.5 <a href="/wiki/Hertz" title="Hertz">GHz</a> <a href="/wiki/Multi-core_processor" title="Multi-core processor">quad-core</a> processor, a display of <a href="/wiki/1080p" title="1080p">1080p</a> (1080×1920 pixels) resolution, a 12-<a href="/wiki/Pixel" title="Pixel">megapixel</a> rear camera and a HD <a href="/wiki/AMOLED#Super_AMOLED_Plus" title="AMOLED">Super AMOLED Plus</a> touchscreen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNET19Mar_32-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNET19Mar-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leak_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leak-33">[33]</a></sup> More accurate rumored specifications included 2 <a href="/wiki/Gibibyte" title="Gibibyte">GB</a> of <a href="/wiki/Random-access_memory" title="Random-access memory">RAM</a>, 64 GB of internal storage, <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a>, a 4.8-inch (120 mm) screen, an 8-megapixel rear camera, and a 9-millimetre (0.35 in) thick chassis.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNET19Mar_32-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNET19Mar-32">[32]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leak_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leak-33">[33]</a></sup> Samsung confirmed the existence of the Galaxy S II's successor on 5 March 2012, but it was not until late April 2012 that Samsung's Senior Vice-President Robert Yi confirmed the phone to be called "Samsung Galaxy S III".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg/220px-Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg/330px-Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg/440px-Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samsung_Mobile_Unpacked_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Galaxy S III's launch at Samsung Mobile Unpacked 2012 (3 May 2012).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After inviting reporters in mid-April, Samsung launched the Galaxy S III during the Samsung Mobile Unpacked 2012 event at <a href="/wiki/Earls_Court_Exhibition_Centre" title="Earls Court Exhibition Centre">Earls Court Exhibition Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, on 3 May 2012, instead of unveiling their products earlier in the year during either the World Mobile Congress or <a href="/wiki/Consumer_Electronics_Show" title="Consumer Electronics Show">Consumer Electronics Show</a> (CES).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMHS3launch_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMHS3launch-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> One explanation for this decision is that Samsung wanted to minimize the time between its launch and availability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCWorld_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-PCWorld-37">[37]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Keynote" title="Keynote">keynote address</a> of the hour-long event was delivered by Loesje De Vriese, <a href="/wiki/Marketing_management" title="Marketing management">Marketing Director</a> of Samsung <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Launch_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Launch-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following the launch of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxy_S4" title="Galaxy S4">Galaxy S4</a> in June 2013, Samsung was reportedly retiring the phone earlier than planned because of low sales numbers and to streamline manufacturing operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Features">Features</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Features">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware_and_design">Hardware and design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Hardware and design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG"><img alt="Photo of two phones turned off held next to each other with warm yellow ambience lightning. The phones are rested on a person's hand." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="960" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG/200px-Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG/300px-Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG/400px-Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galaxy_Nexus_and_Galaxy_S_III_side_by_side.PNG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Nexus" title="Galaxy Nexus">Galaxy Nexus</a> (left) and the Galaxy S III (right)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The S III has a plastic <a href="/wiki/Chassis" title="Chassis">chassis</a> measuring 136.6 mm (5.38 in) long, 70.7 mm (2.78 in) wide, and 8.6 mm (0.34 in) thick, with the device weighing 133 grams (4.7 oz). Samsung abandoned the rectangular design of the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S" title="Samsung Galaxy S">Galaxy S</a> and Galaxy S II, and instead incorporated round corners and curved edges, reminiscent of the <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Nexus" title="Galaxy Nexus">Galaxy Nexus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2012-40">[40]</a></sup> The device has been available in several color options<s>:</s> white, black, grey, blue-grey, red, and brown.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> A "Garnet Red" model was made available exclusively to US carrier <a href="/wiki/AT%26T" title="AT&amp;T">AT&amp;T</a> on 15 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S3Colors_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-S3Colors-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III comes in two distinct variations that differ primarily in the internal hardware. The international S III version has Samsung's <a href="/wiki/Exynos" title="Exynos">Exynos 4 Quad</a> <a href="/wiki/System_on_a_chip" title="System on a chip">system on a chip</a> (SoC) containing a 1.4 GHz quad-core <a href="/wiki/ARM_Cortex-A9" title="ARM Cortex-A9">ARM Cortex-A9</a> <a href="/wiki/Central_processing_unit" title="Central processing unit">central processing unit</a> (CPU) and an <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture" title="ARM architecture">ARM</a> <a href="/wiki/Mali_(GPU)" title="Mali (GPU)">Mali-400 MP</a> <a href="/wiki/Graphics_processing_unit" title="Graphics processing unit">graphics processing unit</a> (GPU).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> According to Samsung, the Exynos 4 Quad doubles the performance of the Exynos 4 Dual used on the S II, while using 20 percent less power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Samsung had also released several <a href="/wiki/4G" title="4G">4G</a> <a href="/wiki/LTE_(telecommunication)" title="LTE (telecommunication)">LTE</a> versions—4G facilitates higher-speed <a href="/wiki/Cellular_network" title="Cellular network">mobile connection</a> compared to <a href="/wiki/3G" title="3G">3G</a>—in selected countries to exploit the corresponding communications infrastructures that exist in those markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M.CCN_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-M.CCN-46">[46]</a></sup> Most of these versions use <a href="/wiki/Qualcomm" title="Qualcomm">Qualcomm</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Snapdragon_S4" title="Snapdragon S4">Snapdragon S4</a> SoC featuring a <a href="/wiki/Multi-core_processor" title="Multi-core processor">dual-core</a> 1.5 GHz <a href="/wiki/Krait_(CPU)" title="Krait (CPU)">Krait</a> CPU and an Adreno 225 GPU.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> The South Korean and Australian versions are a hybrid of the international and 4G-capable versions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-E210S_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-E210S-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III has a maximum of 2 GB of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RAM" title="RAM">RAM</a>, depending on model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-M.CCN_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-M.CCN-46">[46]</a></sup> The phone comes with either 16 or 32 GB of internal storage, with a 64 GB version to be available internationally; additionally, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MicroSDXC" title="MicroSDXC">microSDXC</a> storage offers a further 64 GB for a potential total of 128 GB.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Specs_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Specs-48">[48]</a></sup> Moreover, 50 GB of space is offered for two years on <a href="/wiki/Dropbox_(service)" title="Dropbox (service)">Dropbox</a>—a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_storage" title="Cloud storage">cloud storage</a> service—for purchasers of the device, doubling rival <a href="/wiki/HTC" title="HTC">HTC</a>'s 25 GB storage for the same duration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p12_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p12-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/HD_Super_AMOLED" title="HD Super AMOLED">HD Super AMOLED</a> display measures 4.8 inches (120 mm) on the diagonal. With a 720×1280-pixel (<a href="/wiki/720p" title="720p">720p</a>) resolution, its 306 pixel per inch (PPI, a measure of <a href="/wiki/Pixel_density" title="Pixel density">pixel density</a>) is a relatively high,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Specs_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-Specs-48">[48]</a></sup> which is accommodated by the removal one of the three subpixels—red, green and blue—in each pixel to create a <a href="/wiki/PenTile_matrix_family" title="PenTile matrix family">PenTile matrix</a>-display; consequently, it does not share the "Plus" suffix found on the S II's <a href="/wiki/AMOLED#Super_AMOLED_Plus" title="AMOLED">Super AMOLED Plus</a> display.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNETreview_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNETreview-50">[50]</a></sup> The glass used for the display is the damage-resistant corning <a href="/wiki/Gorilla_Glass" title="Gorilla Glass">Gorilla Glass</a> 2, except for S3 Neo variant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012_40-1"><a href="#cite_note-B2012-40">[40]</a></sup> The device's software includes a feature known as "Smart Stay", which uses the device's front camera to detect whether the user's eyes are looking at the screen, and prevents the screen from automatically turning off while the user is still looking at it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SVoice_SmartStay_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-SVoice_SmartStay-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III has an 8-megapixel camera similar to that of the Galaxy S II. It can take 3264×2448-pixel resolution photos and record videos in 1920×1080-pixel (1080p) resolution. Samsung improved the camera's software over that of its predecessor to include zero <a href="/wiki/Shutter_lag" title="Shutter lag">shutter lag</a>, and Burst Mode and Best Shot, which work together to quickly take numerous photos before the best-judged frame is selected.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p9_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p9-52">[52]</a></sup> The phone can also take pictures while recording videos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNETreview_50-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNETreview-50">[50]</a></sup> The rear-facing camera is complemented by a 1.9-megapixel front-facing camera that can record 720p videos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p9_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p9-52">[52]</a></sup> The phone has <a href="/wiki/Flash_(photography)" title="Flash (photography)">LED flash</a> and <a href="/wiki/Autofocus" title="Autofocus">autofocus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gsmarena1_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-gsmarena1-53">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>In addition to the 4.8-inch (120 mm) touchscreen, the S III has several physical <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/User_input" title="User input">user inputs</a>, including a home button located below the screen, a volume key on the left side and a power/lock key on the right.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UserMan_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-UserMan-55">[55]</a></sup> At the top there is a 3.5-millimetre (0.14 in) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Headphone_jack" title="Headphone jack">headphone jack</a> and one of the two microphones on the S III; the other is located below the home button.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UserMan_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-UserMan-55">[55]</a></sup> The S III is advertised as having an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_High-definition_Link" title="Mobile High-definition Link">MHL</a> port that can be used both as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MicroUSB" title="MicroUSB">micro</a>-<a href="/wiki/USB_On-The-Go" title="USB On-The-Go">USB On-The-Go</a> port, and for connecting the phone to <a href="/wiki/HDMI" title="HDMI">HDMI</a> devices. However, a retailer later discovered that Samsung had made a modification to the electronics of the port such that only the adapter made specifically for this model by Samsung could be used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Galaxy_S3_MHL_explanation_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Galaxy_S3_MHL_explanation-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III's <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">Li-ion</a> 2,100 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ampere-hour" title="Ampere-hour">mAh</a> battery is said to have a 790-hour <a href="/wiki/Sleep_mode" title="Sleep mode">standby time</a> or 11 hours of talk time on 3G, compared to 900 hours in standby and 21 hours of talk time on 2G.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hk-ENSpecs_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hk-ENSpecs-57">[57]</a></sup> Built into the battery is <a href="/wiki/Near_field_communication" title="Near field communication">near field communication</a> (NFC) connectivity, which allows users to share map directions and <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> videos quickly using <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi_Direct" title="Wi-Fi Direct">Wi-Fi Direct</a> (through Android Beam), and perform <a href="/wiki/Contactless_payment" title="Contactless payment">non-touch payments</a> at shops that employ specially equipped NFC <a href="/wiki/Cash_register" title="Cash register">cash registers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The battery can be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wireless_energy_transfer" title="Wireless energy transfer">wirelessly charged</a> using a special charging pad (sold separately) that utilizes magnetic resonance to produce a <a href="/wiki/Magnetic_field" title="Magnetic field">magnetic field</a> through which electricity could be transferred.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CNET_TV" title="CNET TV">CNET TV</a> torture-tested an S III by cooling it to 24 °F (−4 °C), placing it in a heat-proof box and heating it to 190 °F (88 °C), and submerging it in water—the S III survived all three tests. The phone also did not exhibit any scratches when a key was repeatedly scraped against the display.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> However, Android Authority later carried out a drop test with the purpose of comparing the S III and the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_5" title="IPhone 5">iPhone 5</a>. The screen on the S III shattered on the second drop test, while the iPhone received only minor scuffs and scratches on the metal composite frame after three drop tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p><br/></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Software_and_services">Software and services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Software and services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg"><img alt="Rear view of a blue and black phone. A camera lens is located centrally at the top." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1200" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg/170px-Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg/255px-Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg/340px-Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Galaxy_S_III_SC-06D_Pebble_Blue_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Back view of the Japanese S III model, SC-06D</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android (operating system)</a>, <a href="/wiki/TouchWiz" title="TouchWiz">TouchWiz</a>, and <a href="/wiki/S_Voice" title="S Voice">S Voice</a></div>
<p>The S III is powered by Android, a <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a>-based, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_source" title="Open source">open source</a> <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating system</a> developed by Google and introduced commercially in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndroidInc_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-AndroidInc-63">[63]</a></sup> Among other features, the software allows users to maintain customized home screens which can contain shortcuts to applications and <a href="/wiki/Software_widget" title="Software widget">widgets</a> for displaying information. Four shortcuts to frequently used applications can be stored on a dock at the bottom of the screen; the button in the center of the dock opens the application drawer, which displays a menu containing all of the apps installed on the device. A tray accessed by dragging from the top of the screen allows users to view notifications received from other apps, and contains <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Toggle_switch" title="Toggle switch">toggle switches</a> for commonly used functions. Pre-loaded apps also provide access to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_applications" title="Google applications">Google's various services</a>. The S III uses Samsung's proprietary <a href="/wiki/TouchWiz" title="TouchWiz">TouchWiz</a> <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical user interface</a> (GUI). The "Nature" version used by the S III has a more "organic" feel than previous versions, and contains more interactive elements such as a water ripple effect on the <a href="/wiki/Lock_screen" title="Lock screen">lock screen</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Design_story_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Design_story-25">[25]</a></sup> To complement the TouchWiz interface, and as a response to Apple's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siri_(software)" title="Siri (software)">Siri</a>, the phone introduces <a href="/wiki/S_Voice" title="S Voice">S Voice</a>, Samsung's <a href="/wiki/Intelligent_personal_assistant" title="Intelligent personal assistant">intelligent personal assistant</a>. S Voice can recognize eight languages including English, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Korean_(language)" title="Korean (language)">Korean</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_(language)" title="Italian (language)">Italian</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_(language)" title="French (language)">French</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KoreanLaunch_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-KoreanLaunch-64">[64]</a></sup> Based on <a href="/wiki/Vlingo" title="Vlingo">Vlingo</a>, S Voice enables the user to verbally control 20 functions such as playing a song, setting the alarm, or activating driving mode; it relies on <a href="/wiki/Wolfram_Alpha" title="Wolfram Alpha">Wolfram Alpha</a> for online searches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SVoice_SmartStay_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-SVoice_SmartStay-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III initially shipped with <a href="/wiki/Android_version_history" title="Android version history">Android version 4.0.4</a>, named "Ice Cream Sandwich", which became commercially available in March 2012 with the <a href="/wiki/Nexus_S" title="Nexus S">Nexus S</a> and <a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Nexus" title="Galaxy Nexus">Galaxy Nexus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Ice Cream Sandwich has a refined user interface, and expanded camera capabilities, security features and connectivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> In mid-June 2012, Google unveiled <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jelly_Bean_(operating_system)#Android_4.1.x_Jelly_Bean" title="Jelly Bean (operating system)">Android 4.1 "Jelly Bean"</a>, which employs <a href="/wiki/Google_Now" title="Google Now">Google Now</a>, a voice-assistant similar to S Voice, and incorporates other software changes. Samsung accommodated Jelly Bean in the S III by making last-minute hardware changes to the phone in some markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Jelly Bean updates began rolling out to S IIIs in selected European countries, and to the <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile" title="T-Mobile">T-Mobile</a> in the United States in November 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S3JB_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-S3JB-69">[69]</a></sup> Samsung started pushing Android 4.1.2 Jelly Bean to the international version of the S III in December 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> In December 2013, Samsung began rolling out Android 4.3 for the S III, adding user interface features back ported from the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S4" title="Samsung Galaxy S4">Galaxy S4</a>, and support for the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Gear" title="Samsung Galaxy Gear">Samsung Galaxy Gear</a> <a href="/wiki/Smartwatch" title="Smartwatch">smartwatch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4.3UpdateRetry_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-4.3UpdateRetry-8">[8]</a></sup> In March 2014, Samsung started the rollout of 4.4.2 KitKat for the 2 GB variant of the S III.</p>
<p>The S III comes with a multitude of pre-installed <a href="/wiki/Mobile_app" title="Mobile app">applications</a>, including Google Apps like <a href="/wiki/Google_Play" title="Google Play">Google Play</a>, <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google%2B" title="Google+">Google+</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Voice_Search" title="Google Voice Search">Voice Search</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Calendar" title="Google Calendar">Calendar</a>, in addition to Samsung-specific apps such as <a href="/wiki/ChatON" title="ChatON">ChatON</a>, Game Hub, Music Hub, Video Hub, Social Hub and Navigation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UserMan_55-2"><a href="#cite_note-UserMan-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hk-ENSpecs_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hk-ENSpecs-57">[57]</a></sup> To address the fact that iPhone users are reluctant to switch to Android because the OS is not compatible with <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a>, from June 2012 Samsung offered customers of its <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy" title="Samsung Galaxy">Galaxy series</a> the Easy Phone Sync app to enable the transfer of music, photos, videos, <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcasts</a>, and text messages from an iPhone to a Galaxy device.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> The user is able to access Google Play, a <a href="/wiki/Digital_distribution" title="Digital distribution">digital-distribution</a> multimedia-content service exclusive to Android, to download applications, games, music, movies, books, magazines, and TV programs.</p>
<p>Apart from S Voice, Samsung has directed the bulk of the S III's marketing campaign towards the device's <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">"smart" features</a>, which facilitate improved <a href="/wiki/Human%E2%80%93computer_interaction" title="Human–computer interaction">human-device interactivity</a>. These features include: "Direct Call", or the handset's ability to recognise when a user wants to talk to somebody instead of messaging them, if they bring the phone to their head; "Social Tag", a function that identifies and tags people in a photo and shares photos with them; and "Pop Up Play", which allows a video and other applications to occupy the screen at the same time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraphfeatures_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraphfeatures-72">[72]</a></sup> In addition, the S III can beam its screen to a monitor or be used as a remote controller (AllShare Cast and Play) and share photos with people who are tagged in them (Buddy Photo Share).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraphfeatures_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraphfeatures-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Telegraphfeatures_72-2"><a href="#cite_note-Telegraphfeatures-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III can access and play traditional media formats such as music, movies, TV programs, <a href="/wiki/Audiobook" title="Audiobook">audiobooks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Podcast" title="Podcast">podcasts</a>, and can sort its media library alphabetically by song title, artist, <a href="/wiki/Album" title="Album">album</a>, playlist, folder, and <a href="/wiki/Genre" title="Genre">genre</a>. One notable feature of the S III's music player is Music Square, which analyses a song's intensity and ranks the song by mood so that the user can play songs according to their current emotional state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p12_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p12-49">[49]</a></sup> The device also introduced Music Hub, an <a href="/wiki/Online_music_store" title="Online music store">online music store</a> powered by <a href="/wiki/7digital" title="7digital">7digital</a> with a catalogue of over 19 million songs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III was the first smartphone to support <a href="/wiki/Voice_over_LTE" title="Voice over LTE">Voice Over LTE</a> with the introduction of HD Voice service in South Korea.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> The phone enables <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Video_calling" title="Video calling">video calling</a> with its 1.9 MP front-facing camera, and with support for the <a href="/wiki/AptX" title="AptX">aptX</a> <a href="/wiki/Audio_codec" title="Audio codec">codec</a>, improves <a href="/wiki/Bluetooth" title="Bluetooth">Bluetooth</a>-headset connectivity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texting" title="Texting">Texting</a> on the S III does not embody any new significant features from the S II. Speech-to-text is aided by the Vlingo and Google's voice-recognition assistant. Not unlike other Android devices, there are a multitude of third-party typing applications available that could complement the S III's stock keyboard.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 18 June 2012, Samsung announced that the S III would have a version with <a href="/wiki/Enterprise_software" title="Enterprise software">enterprise software</a> under the company's Samsung Approved For Enterprise (SAFE) program, an initiative facilitating the use of its devices for "<a href="/wiki/Bring_your_own_device" title="Bring your own device">bring your own device</a>" scenarios in workplace environments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The enterprise S III version would support <a href="/wiki/Advanced_Encryption_Standard" title="Advanced Encryption Standard">AES-256</a> bit <a href="/wiki/Encryption" title="Encryption">encryption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virtual_private_network" title="Virtual private network">VPN</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mobile_Device_Management" title="Mobile Device Management">Mobile Device Management</a> functionality, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a> <a href="/wiki/Exchange_ActiveSync" title="Exchange ActiveSync">Exchange ActiveSync</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBTSAFE_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-IBTSAFE-78">[78]</a></sup> It was scheduled to be released in the United States in July 2012. The enterprise version was expected to penetrate the business market dominated by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Research_in_Motion" title="Research in Motion">Research in Motion</a>'s <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</a>, following the release of similar enterprise versions of the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_Note_series" title="Samsung Galaxy Note series">Galaxy Note</a>, Galaxy S II and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galaxy_Tab" title="Galaxy Tab">Galaxy Tab</a> line of <a href="/wiki/Tablet_computer" title="Tablet computer">tablet computers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IBTSAFE_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-IBTSAFE-78">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>A separate "Developer Edition" of the S III was made available from Samsung's Developer Portal. It came with an unlockable <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bootloader" title="Bootloader">bootloader</a> to allow the user to modify the phone's software.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Model_variants">Model variants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Model variants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Issues">Issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 19 September 2012, security researchers demonstrated during <a href="/wiki/Pwn2Own" title="Pwn2Own">Pwn2Own</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hacker_(computer_security)" title="Hacker (computer security)">computer hacking</a> contest held in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>, that the S III can be hacked via NFC, allowing attackers to download all data from the phone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2012, two hardware issues were reported by users of the S III: A vulnerability of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exynos_(system_on_chip)" title="Exynos (system on chip)">Exynos SoC</a> allowed malicious apps to gain root privileges even on unrooted devices, and a spontaneous <a href="/wiki/Brick_(electronics)" title="Brick (electronics)">bricking</a> of the unit, called the "sudden death vulnerability", that occurs about six months after activation. Samsung has been replacing the mainboards of affected units under warranty.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> In January 2013, Samsung released a firmware update that corrected both issues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of mid-2013<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, two S III explosions were reported. The first involved a man from <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">Ireland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> while the more recent incident occurred when a Swiss teenager was left with second and third degree burns in her thigh caused by her phone's explosion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2013, Samsung acknowledged swelling and overheating issues with the Li-ion batteries in many S III phones, and offered replacement batteries for affected devices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_reception">Commercial reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Commercial reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to an anonymous Samsung official speaking to the <i><a href="/wiki/Korea_Economic_Daily" title="Korea Economic Daily">Korea Economic Daily</a></i>, the S III received more than 9 million pre-orders from 100 carriers during the two weeks following its London unveiling, making it the fastest-selling <a href="/wiki/Gadget" title="Gadget">gadget</a> in history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9mil_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-9mil-118">[117]</a></sup> In comparison, the <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4S" title="IPhone 4S">iPhone 4S</a> received 4 million pre-orders prior to its launch,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fastestselling_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fastestselling-119">[118]</a></sup> while Samsung's previous flagship phone, the S II, had 10 million handsets shipped within five months. Within a month of the London unveiling, auction and shopping website <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a> noted a 119-percent increase in second-hand Android phone sales. According to an eBay spokesperson, this was "the first time anything other than an Apple product has sparked such a selling frenzy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup></p>
<div class="floatleft">
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_feba87e21d3b6c62148b7e06450adfee" name="timeline_feba87e21d3b6c62148b7e06450adfee"></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/feba87e21d3b6c62148b7e06450adfee.png" usemap="#timeline_feba87e21d3b6c62148b7e06450adfee"/></div>
</div>
<p>The S III was released in 28 countries in Europe and the Middle East on 29 May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCShippingDelays_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-BBCShippingDelays-121">[120]</a></sup> To showcase its flagship device, Samsung afterwards embarked on a global month-long tour of the S III to nine cities, including <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a>, and cities in China, Japan, South Korea and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III has helped Samsung consolidate its <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> in several countries including India, where Samsung expected to capture 60 percent of the country's smartphone market, improving on its previous 46 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IndianS3_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-IndianS3-123">[122]</a></sup> Within a month of release, Samsung had a 60-percent market share in France, while the company controlled over 50 percent of the German and Italian smartphone markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marketshare_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marketshare-124">[123]</a></sup> Over a similar period the S III helped increase Samsung's market share in the United Kingdom to over 40 percent, while eroding the iPhone 4S's 25 percent to 20 percent in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> The S III was scheduled to be released in North America on 20 June 2012, but because of high demand, some US and Canadian carriers delayed the release by several days, while some other carriers limited the market at launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> The S III's US launch event took place in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, hosted by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Twilight_Saga_(film_series)" title="The Twilight Saga (film series)">Twilight</a></i> actress <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Greene" title="Ashley Greene">Ashley Greene</a> and attended by <a href="/wiki/Dubstep" title="Dubstep">dubstep</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Skrillex" title="Skrillex">Skrillex</a>, who performed at Skylight Studios.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Samsung estimated that by the end of July 2012, the S III would have been released by 296 carriers in 145 countries,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReutersS3release_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-ReutersS3release-4">[4]</a></sup> and that more than 10 million handsets would have been sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google.com_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-google.com-128">[127]</a></sup> Shin Jong-kyun, president of Samsung's mobile communications sector, announced on 22 July that sales had exceeded 10 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10mil_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-10mil-129">[128]</a></sup> According to an assessment by Swiss <a href="/wiki/Financial_services" title="Financial services">financial services</a> company <a href="/wiki/UBS" title="UBS">UBS</a>, Samsung had shipped 5–6 million units of the phone in the second quarter of 2012 and would ship 10–12 million handsets per quarter throughout the rest of the year. An even more aggressive prediction by <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>-based banking group <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas" title="BNP Paribas">BNP Paribas</a> said 15 million units will be shipped in the third quarter of 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> while Japanese <a href="/wiki/Financial_adviser" title="Financial adviser">financial consultant</a> company <a href="/wiki/Nomura_Group" title="Nomura Group">Nomura</a> placed the figure for this quarter as high as 18 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> Sales of the S III were estimated to top 40 million by the end of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> To meet demand, Samsung had hired 75,000 workers, and its South Korean factory was running at its peak capacity of 5 million smartphone units per month.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9mil_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-9mil-118">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<p>A manufacturing flaw resulted in a large portion of the new smartphones having irregularities with the "hyper-glazing" process. The mistake caused an undesirable finish on the blue back covers and resulted in the disposal of up to 600,000 plastic casings and a shortage of the blue model.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Geek_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-Geek-17">[17]</a></sup> The issue was later resolved; however, <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> estimated that the shortage had cost Samsung two million S III sales during its first month of release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 6 September 2012, Samsung revealed that sales of the S III had reached 20 million in 100 days, making it three and six times faster-selling than the Galaxy S II and the Galaxy S, respectively. Europe accounted for more than 25 percent of this figure with 6 million units, followed by Asia (4.5 million) and the US (4 million); sales in South Korea, the S III's home market, numbered 2.5 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100days20mil_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-100days20mil-15">[15]</a></sup> Around the same time of Samsung's announcement, sales of the S III surpassed that of the iPhone 4S in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the third quarter of 2012, more than 18 million S III units were shipped, making it the most popular smartphone at the time, ahead of the iPhone 4S's 16.2 million units. Analysts deduced that the slump in iPhone sales was due to customers' anticipation of the iPhone 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup></p>
<p>By May 2014, the S III had sold approximately 60 million units since its 2012 release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup> In April 2015, the total sales number was reported as 70 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-computerworld_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-computerworld-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 October 2012 Samsung unveiled the <a href="/wiki/Samsung_Galaxy_S_III_Mini" title="Samsung Galaxy S III Mini">Galaxy S III Mini</a>, a 4-inch (100 mm) smartphone with lower specifications compared to the S III.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The reception of the S III has been particularly positive. Critics noted the phone's blend of features, such as its S Voice application, display, processing speed, and dimensions as having an edge over its competition, the Apple <a href="/wiki/IPhone_4S" title="IPhone 4S">iPhone 4S</a> and <a href="/wiki/HTC_One_X" title="HTC One X">HTC One X</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012_40-2"><a href="#cite_note-B2012-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNETreview_50-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNETreview-50">[50]</a></sup> Vlad Savov of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Verge_(website)" title="The Verge (website)">The Verge</a></i> declared it a "technological triumph",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> while Natasha Lomas of <a href="/wiki/CNET" title="CNET">CNET UK</a> lauded the phone's "impossibly slim and light casing and a quad-core engine", calling it the "Ferrari of Android phones",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNETreview_50-3"><a href="#cite_note-CNETreview-50">[50]</a></sup> a sentiment affirmed ("a prince among Android phones") by Dave Oliver of <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_UK" title="Wired UK">Wired UK</a></i> and ("king of Android") Esat Dedezade of <a href="/wiki/Stuff_(magazine)" title="Stuff (magazine)"><i>Stuff</i> magazine</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> Gareth Beavis of <a href="/wiki/TechRadar" title="TechRadar">TechRadar</a> noted that the S III is "all about faster, smarter and being more minimal than ever before while keeping the spec list at the bleeding edge of technology."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p18_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p18-142">[141]</a></sup> Matt Warman of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> said, "On spending just a short time with the S3, I'm confident in saying that it's a worthy successor to the globally popular S2".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Upon release, a number of critics and publications have made references to the S III, Samsung's 2012 <a href="/wiki/Core_product" title="Core product">flagship phone</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> as an "iPhone killer",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iPhonekiller1_145-0"><a href="#cite_note-iPhonekiller1-145">[144]</a></sup> responding perhaps to Apple's favourable customer perception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> The label owes itself to the S III's use of the Android OS—the chief rival of Apple's <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a>—as well as its design and features that rival the iPhone 4S such as Smart Stay, a large display, a quad-core processor, Android customizability, and a multitude of connectivity options.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup></p>
<p>The S III was the first Android phone to have a higher launch price than the iPhone 4S when the Apple product was released in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> With the S III, Tim Weber, business editor of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, observed, "With the new Galaxy S3 they [Samsung] have clearly managed to move to the front of the smartphone field, ahead of mighty Apple itself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBCShippingDelays_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-BBCShippingDelays-121">[120]</a></sup></p>
<p>Conversely, reviewers have opined on the design and feel of phone, calling its polycarbonate shell "cheap"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> and having a "slippery feel".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p18_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p18-142">[141]</a></sup> The S Voice was described as "not optimised" and "more rigid than Siri" with its poor <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">voice-recognition</a> accuracy, with instances when it would not respond at all.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-B2012p18_142-2"><a href="#cite_note-B2012p18-142">[141]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> Another usage problem was a microphone malfunction that resulted in difficulty communicating during a call.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup> Reviewers have noted the somewhat abrupt auto-adjustment of display brightness, which tends to under-illuminate the screen;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[N 2]</a></sup> however, it has twice the battery life compared to the HTC handset, achieved partly through the dim display.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PCA_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-PCA-154">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[N 3]</a></sup> Others say the numerous pre-installed apps make the S III feel "<a href="/wiki/Software_bloat" title="Software bloat">bloated</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloat_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloat-156">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[N 4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In late-September 2012 TechRadar ranked it as the No. 1 handset in its constantly updated list of the 20 best mobile phones;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Beavis.2C_Gareth_18-1"><a href="#cite_note-Beavis.2C_Gareth-18">[18]</a></sup> <i>Stuff</i> magazine also ranked it at No. 1 in its list of 10 best smartphones in May 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Top_10_Smartphones_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-Top_10_Smartphones-19">[19]</a></sup> The S III won an award from the <a href="/wiki/European_Imaging_and_Sound_Association" title="European Imaging and Sound Association">European Imaging and Sound Association</a> under the category of "European Mobile Phone" of 2012–2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mobile_Devices_Awards_History_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mobile_Devices_Awards_History-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2012, the S III won <i>T3'</i>s "Phone of the Year" award, beating the iPhone 4S, the <a href="/wiki/Nokia_Lumia_900" title="Nokia Lumia 900">Nokia Lumia 900</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Sony_Xperia_S" title="Sony Xperia S">Sony Xperia S</a> and others<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Future_Publishing_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Future_Publishing-21">[21]</a></sup> and was voted Phone of the Year by readers of tech website S21.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S21_Phone_of_the_Year_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-S21_Phone_of_the_Year-158">[154]</a></sup> In February 2013, the S III won the "Best Smartphone" award from the <a href="/wiki/GSMA" title="GSMA">GSMA</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mobile_World_Congress" title="Mobile World Congress">Mobile World Congress</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Litigation">Litigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samsung_Galaxy_S_III&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Litigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 5 June 2012, Apple filed for <a href="/wiki/Preliminary_injunction" title="Preliminary injunction">preliminary injunctions</a> in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_District_Court_for_the_Northern_District_of_California" title="United States District Court for the Northern District of California">United States District Court for the Northern District of California</a> against Samsung Electronics, claiming the S III had violated at least two of the company's <a href="/wiki/Patent" title="Patent">patents</a>. Apple requested that the court include the phone in its existing legal battle against Samsung (see <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apple_Inc._v._Samsung_Electronics_Co.,_Ltd." title="Apple Inc. v. Samsung Electronics Co., Ltd.">Apple Inc. v. Samsung Electronics Co., Ltd.</a></i>), and ban sales of the S III prior to its scheduled 21 June 2012 US launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[157]</a></sup> Apple claimed the alleged infringements would "cause immediate and irreparable harm" to its commercial interest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW.de_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-DW.de-162">[158]</a></sup> Samsung responded by declaring it would "vigorously oppose the request and demonstrate to the court that the Galaxy S3 [<i><a href="/wiki/Sic" title="Sic">sic</a></i>] is innovative and distinctive", and reassured the public that 21 June release would proceed as planned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DW.de_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-DW.de-162">[158]</a></sup> On 11 June, Judge <a href="/wiki/Lucy_H._Koh" title="Lucy H. Koh">Lucy Koh</a> said that Apple's claim would overload her work schedule, as she would also be overseeing the trial of Samsung's other devices; consequently, Apple dropped its request to block 21 June release of the S III.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[159]</a></sup></p>
<p>In mid-July 2012, Samsung removed the universal search feature on Sprint and AT&amp;T S III phones with <a href="/wiki/Over-the-air_programming" title="Over-the-air programming">over-the-air</a> (OTA) software updates to disable the local search function as a "precautionary measure" prior to its patent court trial with Apple, which began on 30 July 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[160]</a></sup> Although Apple won the trial, the S III experienced a sales spike because of the public's belief that the phone would be banned.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[161]</a></sup> On 31 August 2012, Apple asked the same federal court to add the S III into its existing complaint, believing the device has violated its patents. Samsung countered with the statement: "Apple continues to resort to litigation over market competition in an effort to limit consumer choice."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[162]</a></sup></p>

Samsung Electronics<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">15 June</span> 2012</span>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASamsung+Galaxy+S+III&amp;rft.btitle=Samsung+Galaxy+S+III&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.samsung.com%2Fglobal%2Fgalaxys3%2F&amp;rft.pub=Samsung+Electronics&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
